Provisional Regulations for Three Types of Passports Issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

The Shanghai Special Municipality Government received the provisional regulations for three types of passports issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and hereby appends them as follows:

Provisional Regulations for Exit Passports Issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Article 1: Exit passports are divided into three types: diplomatic passports, official passports, and ordinary passports. Article 2: Diplomatic passports are applicable to the following personnel: 1. The Chairman of the National Government and their family members; 2. Members of the Central Party Headquarters' Executive and Supervisory Committees and their family members; 3. Members of the National Government, Presidents and Vice-Presidents of various Yuan (branches of government), Ministers of various Ministries, Chairmen of various Commissions, and their family members; 4. Diplomatic and consular officials and their family members; 5. Staff members of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and their family members; 6. Personnel dispatched by the National Government to various countries' governments and international organizations on official business, as well as special couriers; 7. Attendants of the above items. Article 3: Official passports are applicable to civil servants of central and local government agencies other than those specified in the preceding article. Article 4: Ordinary passports are applicable to citizens who go abroad for study, business, work, or travel. Article 5: Exit passports shall be formulated and issued by the Ministry. Article 6: Diplomatic passports shall be obtained from the Ministry. Official and ordinary passports may be obtained from the Ministry or from municipal and county governments designated by the Ministry. Article 7: Exit passports shall be in triplicate form, with the original copy given to the passport holder, and in the case of issuance by municipal and county governments designated by the Ministry, one copy shall be reported to the Ministry for verification and one copy shall be kept by the issuing agency for reference. All entries shall be made in accordance with the passport number. Article 8: Applicants for exit passports shall pay a fee of six yuan per passport, with students and workers paying half price. In addition, three recent 4.5-inch head-and-shoulder photographs shall be affixed to the passport and the stub, and stamp duty shall be paid in accordance with the Stamp Tax Regulations of the Ministry of Finance (one yuan for passports for overseas study, including officials and businessmen; two yuan for passports for overseas travel, including officials and businessmen; and three jiao for passports for overseas labor). However, diplomatic passports are exempt from fees. Article 9: Applicants for exit passports shall first fill out an application form for exit passports. When applying for an ordinary passport, the passport applicant shall also submit a request letter, together with the following guarantee documents, for approval by the issuing agency: For overseas business, a guarantee letter from the local chamber of commerce or two reputable business firms, proving the amount of capital; for overseas work, a guarantee letter from the local labor union or two reputable business firms, proving the applicant's work skills; for overseas study, prior approval from the Ministry of Education or the Training Directorate-General shall be obtained in accordance with regulations, and the approval documents shall be submitted for verification; for overseas travel, a guarantee letter from the local statutory authority, guaranteeing that the applicant will not engage in any business activities after going abroad. Article 10: Upon arrival at the overseas destination, the passport holder shall present the passport to the local or nearby Chinese embassy or consulate for registration. Article 11: Passports are valid for one year. Upon expiration, if the passport holder wishes to continue residing abroad, the old passport shall be presented to the local or nearby Chinese embassy or consulate for cancellation and a new passport shall be obtained in exchange, with fees paid in accordance with regulations. Expired passports not renewed shall be invalid. Article 12: If the passport holder's passport is lost or damaged, a guarantee letter shall be obtained and a new passport shall be applied for from the issuing agency or the local or nearby Chinese embassy or consulate, with fees paid in accordance with regulations. In the event of a lost passport, the passport holder shall publish a declaration of invalidation in the newspaper. In the event of a damaged passport, it shall be presented for cancellation before a new passport can be exchanged. Article 13: If the passport holder wishes to go abroad again after returning to the country, a new passport shall be applied for separately. Article 14: If it is found that the passport does not match the person after the passport is issued, the passport shall be cancelled and the holder ordered to return to the country. Article 15: If the issuing agency privately prints and issues passports, it shall be strictly investigated in accordance with the law. Article 16: The issuing agency shall, every three months, prepare a register of passport stubs and fees collected and submit them to the Ministry, and shall be allowed to deduct 20% of the fees for office expenses. Article 17: The issuing agency shall, when issuing passports, pay attention to the regulations of various countries regarding the entry of foreigners. Article 18: The

Page 14

matter list, the request letter, and the guarantee letter stipulated in these regulations shall be printed and issued by the Ministry, and the passport applicant may obtain them from the issuing agency. Article 19: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 20: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Provisional Regulations for the Issuance of Return Passports by Chinese Embassies and Consulates Abroad and the Visa of Foreigners' Passports to China: Article 1: Citizens residing abroad shall, before returning to the country, apply to the local or nearby Chinese embassy or consulate for a return passport. The return passport shall be in triplicate form, with the original copy given to the passport holder, one copy reported to the Ministry for verification, and one copy kept by the embassy or consulate for reference. All entries shall be made in accordance with the passport number. Return passports shall be formulated and issued by the Ministry. Article 2: Applicants for return passports shall present their passports issued when they went abroad before they can be issued. This does not apply to children of overseas Chinese born abroad and naturalized persons. Article 3: Applicants for return passports shall pay a fee of six yuan per passport, with students and workers paying half price. In addition, three recent 4.5-inch head-and-shoulder photographs shall be affixed to the passport and the stub, and stamp duty shall be paid in accordance with the Stamp Tax Regulations of the Ministry of Finance (two yuan for travel passports, including officials and businessmen; one yuan for study passports; and three jiao for overseas labor passports). However, diplomatic passports are exempt from fees. Article 4: Chinese embassies and consulates abroad shall, if it is found that applicants for return passports are carrying prohibited items, notify the customs authorities at the port of entry to investigate. Article 5: Return passports shall become invalid upon return to the country after being issued. Article 6: When foreigners request a visa for their passport to China, it shall be submitted by the foreign diplomatic agency or local competent authority to the Chinese embassy or consulate stationed in that area for visa. If a private individual submits a visa request directly, it shall be introduced by a legitimate practitioner of that country. Article 7: Foreigners requesting a visa for their passports shall fill out two copies of the visa application form and pay the visa fee in accordance with the provisions of the following article. When issuing visas, the embassies and consulates shall prepare a triplicate certificate, with one copy and one copy of the application form reported to the Ministry for verification, one copy reported to the embassy, and the remaining copy and one copy of the application form kept in the embassy for reference (if the visa is issued at the embassy, only two copies of the triplicate certificate shall be filled out). Article 8: The visa fees collected by Chinese embassies and consulates abroad shall be collected by comparing the visa passport fees of embassies and consulates of various countries stationed in China. However, diplomatic passports are exempt from fees. Article 9: Chinese embassies and consulates abroad shall refuse to issue a visa if it is found that an applicant is carrying prohibited items. If it is discovered after the visa has been issued, the customs authorities at the port of entry shall be notified to investigate. Article 10: Citizens who return to the country without a return passport and foreigners who come to China without a visa from a Chinese embassy or consulate shall be detained by the customs authorities at the port of entry for investigation. Article 11: Chinese embassies and consulates abroad handling return passports and visas for foreigners to China shall, every three months, prepare a register of passport stubs, visa application forms, and visa certificates, together with all fees collected, and submit them to the Ministry, and shall be allowed to deduct 20% of the fees for office expenses. Article 12: Chinese embassies and consulates abroad handling passport issuance and visas that privately print and issue passports or issue visas in violation of these regulations shall be strictly investigated. Article 13: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 14: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Departure for Belgium on April 5th

Farewell Banquets from All Walks of Life for Days

Mr. Chu Minyi, the representative of our country to the Belgian Exposition, is scheduled to depart for Belgium on April 5th, accompanied by Mr. Xu Shiqi, Special Commissioner of the Ministry of Health, Mr. Zou Fusong, an electrical engineering expert, Mr. Zhou Shida, a secretary, and Mr. Jin Shoufeng, a Taijiquan instructor, on the French postal ship Athos II. The Land Bureau Measures Tangqiao District

The Municipal Land Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Notice is hereby given that the Bureau is now beginning to measure the land of the 12th and 13th Tu households in the 24th Bao of Tangqiao District. Landowners should pay attention to the following items: (1) The dibao (local wardens) will distribute the insurance forms to the landowners. The landowners should fill them out truthfully within ten days after receiving the forms and return them to the dibao for collection and submission to the Bureau's Measurement Team 1, or the landowners can submit them directly to the Measurement Team. (2) Those who have not received the forms due to the landowners' addresses being unknown may submit them to the Bureau's Measurement Team 1 themselves. (3) Landowners whose land deeds are mortgaged and cannot fill out the name and mu (unit of land) on the form should immediately copy them from the mortgagees and not make excuses. (4) When the landowners' land is measured, the landowners must, together with the dibao, clearly point out the boundaries to the surveyors or measurers, or entrust a representative to point out the boundaries on the spot in advance. Otherwise, the Bureau will only rely on the dibao's instructions, and the landowners will be responsible for any errors or disputes in the future. The above four items are all related to the landowners' consolidation of property rights. Please pay special attention to this notice."

British Authorities Crack Down on Private Postal Agencies' Bulk Mail

Ministry of Communications Cables Instruct Explanation of Misunderstanding

Shantou and Xiamen Commissioners Handle Matter with Utmost Care

The news of the British authorities in Kuala Lumpur planning to crack down on private postal agencies' bulk mail within a specified time limit has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now reported that the Chinese Postal Service, after receiving the letter from Kuala Lumpur Post Office, limiting the implementation of the crackdown after March 31, and enclosing notices from the governments of various islands in the South Seas and the Federated Malay States, immediately reported it to the Ministry of Communications, ordering them to explain it to overseas Chinese groups in Shanghai and other places to avoid misunderstandings, and to instruct the commissioners sent to Shantou and Xiamen to handle the matter quickly and carefully. As the time limit for the British postal service's crackdown is imminent, and a solution is urgently needed, the General Bureau has appointed commissioners Zhou Huodong and Lin Zhuowu to go to the Chinese Overseas Chinese Federation, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and other organizations to explain the situation and ask for their support, and has scheduled to go to Shantou and Xiamen tomorrow to contact and handle matters with the relevant parties, so as to take into account both the International Postal Union Convention and the convenience of overseas Chinese communications, and to handle the matter carefully. Attached is the Ministry's cable: "Shanghai Postal Service General Bureau Office, all telegrams and submissions from the view of Ge Dai and Zhong are known. Regarding the case of cracking down on private postal agencies' bulk mail, since a reply from the British Kuala Lumpur Post Office has been received proving that it was not proposed by our country, please explain it clearly to the overseas Chinese groups in Shanghai and other places to avoid misunderstandings, and instruct the commissioners sent to Shantou and Xiamen to handle the matter quickly and carefully. In addition to reporting the actual situation to the government and notifying the relevant agencies, and replying to the various organizations in Singapore by telegram, the cable is followed, Ministry of Communications Ma Yin."

Singapore Cracks Down on Private Postal Agencies

Postal General Bureau Mistakenly Believes Kuala Lumpur

Yesterday, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce sent a telegram to the National Government, stating: "To the Nanjing National Government Junjian, regarding the case of the Ministry of Communications Postal General Bureau initiating the cancellation of overseas Chinese mail bulk mail, the subordinate association has telegraphed to your government to order the Ministry to cancel it. On March 22 of this year, a letter from the Secretariat of the Civil Service of your government on March 19 was received, approving the Ministry of Communications' reply, stating that the Postal General Bureau's presentation stated that the reports were untrue, and that the Kuala Lumpur Postal General Bureau had been telegraphed, and a reply was received stating that the bureau did not say to the representatives when the Chinese representatives petitioned the Governor of Singapore, etc., that the Postal General Bureau of China initiated the crackdown, etc., and that the Ministry of Communications copied the two letters to the association for reference, etc. After checking the Shanghai Shen Bao reported on February 26, the words 'China initiated the crackdown' were what the Singapore Governor's Chinese Civil Affairs Secretary and the Postal Governor said to the Chinese representatives Li Weinan, etc., and presented the Postal General Bureau's repeated letters as

General Bureau, the location and the organization do not match, resulting in the letter being irrelevant, and the general representative of the entire overseas Chinese convention petitioning for the retention of the private postal agencies in Singapore, Li Weinan, is the current chairman of the Singapore Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, and Lin Yishun is the former chairman of the Singapore Chinese General Chamber of Commerce. The two general representatives Li and Lin repeatedly telegraphed your government and the Ministry of Communications, all stating the details of this matter. If the Postal General Bureau of the Ministry of Communications did not initiate the crackdown, the Governor of Singapore, etc., would not dare to announce it, and there would be no repeated letters presented as evidence. If the Governor of Singapore, etc., did not say this, then the two general representatives Li and Lin would not dare to put it in official documents. This case is of great importance to increasing the suffering of the overseas Chinese compatriots. Therefore, we are sending another telegram to your government for verification, and we request that you approve the telegram to the Consul General in Singapore, the Singapore Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, and the Singapore General Branch of our Party to investigate and reply together to distinguish right from wrong and clarify responsibilities. We still earnestly request the retention of the private postal agency method to sympathize with the difficulties of the overseas Chinese. We cannot bear the urgent waiting for orders."

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities previously established public advertising spaces in various locations, mostly leaving space at the bottom for merchants to post paper advertisements and for Party, government, and military agencies to post notices. The Wusong Chamber of Commerce Requests a Reduction in Ship Tax

Yesterday's Reply to the Port Authority

Since the Shanghai Special Municipality Finance Bureau and the Port Authority established a household registration office in Wusong to collect ship tax, the boatmen from Taizhou, Chongming, Haimen, Ningbo, Shaoxing, Shandong, and other places have opposed it and have requested the Wusong Chamber of Commerce to report the situation. The Municipal Finance Bureau sympathetically took into account the shipping merchants' concerns and agreed to reduce the tax burden appropriately. Subsequently, Zheng Shushan, chairman of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, attended a meeting convened by the Port Authority and explained in detail the difficulties of the various ship merchants, requesting a reduction in the tax. After discussion, it was decided that ships carrying sand, gravel, firewood, and charcoal would pay one yuan each time, regardless of size, and that the methods for other types of sailboats would be determined after investigation. Then it was decided to follow the plan. A few days ago, the Wusong Chamber of Commerce suddenly received a letter from the Port Authority stating that the situation described by Chairman Zheng of your Chamber was inconsistent with the findings of the Municipal Finance Bureau, and therefore it was not possible to implement the plan and the tax must still be paid according to the regulations. It is now learned that the Chamber of Commerce believes that the situation presented at the Port Authority meeting last time was entirely factual, and since it has been decided, it should naturally be implemented according to the plan and the previous decision cannot be overturned. Today, the Municipal Finance Bureau's investigation of the number of ships does not match. It is not known what the basis is. Furthermore, when various ships enter the port, the Shadiaochuan Tax Bureau collects ship tax, and they are also required to pay to the ship household registration office, which is equivalent to collecting the tax twice. The ship households' strength is unbearable. Therefore, reducing the tax rate according to the previous agreement, the ship households may be able to reluctantly accept it. If the Municipal Finance Bureau's current proposed method must be implemented for collection, then the ship households will find it difficult to bear, and it is feared that the reconciliation will not be successful and the shipping merchants will go to other ports, and the commerce of Songkou will decline completely. Therefore, the above situation was replied to the Port Authority yesterday (the letter is omitted), requesting that it be forwarded to the Municipal Finance Bureau, and that it consider the people's livelihood and sympathize with the hard-working shipping merchants, and continue to implement the method decided last time, so as to take into account both the treasury tax and the people's livelihood.

Dr. Eddy Gave a Speech at the General Labor Union the Other Day

Titled "The Situation of Laborers in the World"

The Shanghai Special Municipality General Labor Union Preparatory Committee invited Dr. Eddy of the United States to give a speech at 2:00 p.m. the other day (24th). A total of two hundred and several dozen representatives attended. The chairman was Lu Jingshi, the recorders were Yuan Zhaoxin and Shao Yida, and the master of ceremonies was Yu Yaoqiu. First, the chairman introduced Dr. Eddy, followed by Dr. Eddy's speech, titled "The Current Situation of Laborers in the World," which was translated by Huang Chuntao. The gist of his speech is as follows: Today, I and many labor leaders meet here, and the meeting place is full of a new atmosphere, which is very gratifying and the most hopeful thing. In twenty years, I have been to China seven times. I plan to travel around the world in thirty-five years. Now, I will talk about the four countries I have personally visited: the United States, Britain, Russia, and India. Finally, I will talk about the labor industry in China. The wages in the United States are the highest, and workers' insurance is also complete. Most of them pay attention to large-scale labor movements. Capitalists also have organized organizations, such as medical care and bathing, which the capitalists regard as charitable in nature. Workers at the Ford Motor Company used to earn five gold dollars a day, but now it has increased. There are two people in the British labor movement who are struggling: one is McDonald. Their organization is very powerful. It is not a tool for changing government but is really for the happiness of workers. Later, the Labor Party was organized, and the Labor Party had a Ministry of Finance, a Ministry of the Interior, and an Economic Custodial Department, which was very powerful. It also stipulates the wages of laborers, at least how much insurance, and all other workers have reached an extremely high level, which I admire very much. Later, I went to Russia. The Russian problem is very difficult to talk about, because their country is the only country in the world, so there are people who are optimistic and pessimistic about heaven and hell. What I want to talk about is all the places I have seen. Their leaders are the same as ordinary people. If there are people who have irregular behaviors such as prostitution and concubinage, they will immediately use the most severe methods to punish them, such as exile. Their country is the poorest, and the wages of laborers are the lowest. In the United States, each person earns five yuan a day, but they only earn one yuan. Once, I saw 300,000 workers in a large cement factory resting in the garden, very happy. The library and hygiene facilities inside are all available and free of charge. In the factory, important matters, as well as education newspapers, etc., will be closed immediately if they are considered incorrect, as well as movies that should or should not be promoted. Managing the government is especially their main task. As for those who are exiled, they cannot come back again. It is estimated that there are also tens of hundreds of thousands of people who have been exiled, which is what I do not approve of. When I went to India, I saw a strange person, Gandhi, who talked about universal love and asked to use sincere love to influence people. I was with him for three days. He was very poor and lived a very simple life. He did not have a salary of three yuan and seventy-five jiao. He only ate some porridge and milk and wore rough clothes every day, which he made himself. Five hundred thousand people listened to his speech. His peaceful methods won the trust of the masses. The Chinese people account for a quarter of the world. Generally speaking, India is more bitter than China. In fact, China is more bitter than India. I hope you will unite to seek the liberation of the whole. In short, it is easier for capitalists to do things. What can workers do? In Britain, I saw an industrialist whose heart was to enable workers to get decent wages, to be able to marry themselves, and to enable their children to get a decent education. In the factory, they work forty hours a week, and there is employment insurance, etc. Workers who are unemployed still have decent wages, and workers also have the right to speak in the management of the enterprise. In the five years of the European War, he earned millions of dividends and distributed them all to the workers. He went to the capital because his brother could seek knowledge, but workers could not do it, and one party could not have high knowledge, so it is necessary to improve the workers. I hope everyone will unite and work for the welfare of the workers, so that the labor movement is in a good condition. The labor movement is not a tool of politicians. Some people use workers to strike in order to achieve their own goals, which is suicide. The labor movement is entirely in the hands of the workers and should have intelligent and clever leaders, because the labor movement is the most sacred. It is wrong to be loyal to the country but not to the labor movement. I have been to China in the Qing Dynasty, during the Boxer Rebellion, and also during the Yuan Shikai era. The current phenomenon in China is better than before, but I hope you have the power to stop military action and pay special attention to the people's livelihood in the Three Principles of the People. For the whole world, we must also regard it as one body. This is your responsibility, and so on.

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, concerned about the lack of specific regulations in China for merchants initiating joint-stock companies and soliciting stock subscriptions, which often leads to fraudulent stock offerings and deceptive practices, has decided to strictly crack down on these abuses to prevent further problems. County Public Security Bureau Rectifies Police Regulations

Zhao Lian, the Chief Inspector of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, recently noted the lax discipline among the police officers in the bureau. Their uniforms and weapons were often unbuttoned and rusty, and many officers did not reside in the dormitories after their night shifts. Fearing that this would lead to corruption among the police force, he has issued the following order to all police officers in order to rectify the police regulations: It is hereby announced that the spirit of the police lies entirely in their neat and tidy appearance. If their uniforms are not in order, their spirit is completely extinguished. The police are the role models for the people, and should strive to be more diligent and eliminate bad habits in order to fulfill their duty. On the 20th of this month, at 8:40 PM, it was observed that only two officers were on duty at the main gate, one officer was missing, one was armed, and one was unarmed. All were wearing cotton overcoats, and the buttons on the armed officer's overcoat were mostly missing. Both inner and outer garments were unbuttoned, and the rifle was covered in rust. The ammunition belt was also not worn, and the officers stood with no spirit. Such a situation is equivalent to wooden puppets and is extremely unsightly. The post downstairs at the county government building was not seen, presumably having been removed long ago. Upon inspecting the patrol officers' dormitories, many were not in their rooms, and it is unknown where they were idling. How can they assemble in case of an emergency? As the Chief Inspector responsible for inspection and command, I must make a vigorous effort to rectify this situation and rejuvenate the force, thereby enhancing the reputation of our Public Security Department. It is hereby ordered that the patrol officers properly supervise and restrain the long-term officers in the bureau, and instruct all officers to clean and organize their uniforms and weapons by a specific date to improve their appearance. The patrol officers' etiquette must be practiced diligently, and no further signs of corruption should be seen. Furthermore, after investigating, it was found that five agencies are located within this compound, all sharing the same main gate for entry and exit. The security responsibility is extremely important. Not only must uniforms be neat and tidy, but all matters must also be handled with care to avoid negligence. Hereafter, those found with untidy uniforms, unbuttoned buttons, unauthorized absence from duty, or leaving without permission at night will be severely punished to enforce police regulations.

Machine Factory: Young Master Abducted by Bandits

Bandits Trick Apprentice into Opening Door

Robbery of Over One Hundred Silver Dollars

Three-Year-Old Son Abducted

Wang Shunjin, a native of Ningbo, 47 years old, runs the Tongshunxing Machine Factory at No. 515-6, Alley 2, Jingwei Road, Fair Road. His residence is next door to the factory. Last night, around 8:40 PM, the alley gate was closed and guarded by an apprentice named Rui Di. Suddenly, someone knocked on the door, calling out Rui Di's name. The apprentice immediately opened the gate and let the person in. It turned out to be a group of seven or eight burly men, some wearing long robes and others short jackets. They went straight into No. 535. Wang Shunjin's wife and children were chatting in the living room. Two bandits stood guard outside, while the others entered the room, pulled out pistols, and spoke in a Qingjiang accent, telling everyone in the room not to move. They then invaded the inner room, ransacked the chests and cabinets, and stole 106 silver dollars. However, the bandits' goal was not just money. As they left, they snatched Wang Shunjin's three-year-old second son, Xia Sheng, from the arms of the maid, and fled.

Truth Behind the Double Suicide Case

Unable to Marry Prostitute Due to Poverty

Left with No Other Option

Lu Fengzhi's Real Name is Huizhu

Deceased Left Behind Elderly Mother

Guo Jinhua, a native of Zhongshan, Guangdong, and a woman named Lu Fengzhi, also from Zhongshan, experienced difficulties in their love affair and were unable to achieve their desired union. They decided to commit suicide together. They checked into Room 447 of a hotel on Nanjing Road and consumed poison together, hoping to die together. The tea server discovered them, and Guo had already succumbed to the poison, with no hope of recovery. He died at the scene. Miss Lu was still salvageable and was taken to Guangren Hospital for treatment by the police. Guo's body was taken to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road to await official examination. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Guo Jinhua, the deceased, worked at a certain bank during his lifetime. His family was poor, and his monthly salary was barely enough to make ends meet. However, he suddenly lost his job at the end of the year before last and has been unemployed ever since. Guo had six brothers who often came to comfort him. Last spring, he and his friends frequented brothels. Because the madam, Lu Zhang, at the Guangdong prostitute house No. 209, Renzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road, treated Guo very well, Guo lingered at her house. The madam, nearly forty years old, had a husband who did not have a proper job, so she had no choice but to have her biological daughter, Huizhu, engage in prostitution to make a living. Huizhu, seventeen years old, was charming and amiable. Seeing that Guo was gentle and refined, she was willing to devote herself to him. The madam was also happy to have this potential son-in-law, so she allowed her daughter to be in love with Guo, unlike other madams who were only interested in profit. Huizhu removed her name from the list of prostitutes this year and waited exclusively for Guo to marry her. However, Guo was plagued by poverty and had not been able to make it a reality. As time went on, he became desperate, and Huizhu pressed him further. Guo then invited the woman to a hotel, where they confided in each other in a private room and he expressed his desire to commit suicide. The woman could not bear to abandon Guo and agreed to commit suicide with him. Thus, they took poison together. When they first arrived at the hotel, Guo used the alias Huang Zhihua, and the woman used the alias Lu Zhifen. After the incident, Guo's real name was discovered from a name card found on his person, and the woman's name, Huizhu, was also discovered by the police after she was sent to the hospital. Yesterday morning, Judge Gao Junxiang of the Provisional Court came to the scene to examine the body and took his seat in the public chamber. The hotel tea server, Lou Yongfa, described in detail the process of how the young couple entered the hotel and were discovered to have taken poison. Guo's mother, Guo Li, requested permission to claim the body for burial and stated that she still did not know why her son committed suicide. Huizhu's mother, Lu Zhang, was also summoned to court and testified that Guo frequented her establishment, developed a love affair with her daughter, and that his suicide was due to his inability to marry her. She said that Guo had attempted suicide three times before for this reason, but was discovered each time. Judge Gao then instructed Guo Li to arrange for the burial. Guo, who was willing to abandon his elderly mother and commit suicide for the sake of a prostitute, although his intentions were extremely foolish and not to be imitated, his situation is indeed very pitiful.

Lawyer's Fee Issue in Property Dispute Case

Xi Yafu vs. Ma Ma

Both Parties Agreed to a Contract at the Time of Engagement

30% of Proceeds to be Paid as Remuneration

Settlement Reached, Securing Assets of 10,000 Yuan

Lawyer's Fees Demanded, But Refused

The Jinlingchun Restaurant on Zhengjia Muqiao, is owned by the Ma family. There are five Ma brothers, the eldest of whom is deceased, leaving behind his wife, Mrs. Ma. Recently, Mrs. Ma was involved in a property dispute in the Provisional Court with her uncles-in-law, Ma Houji, Hounian, Houwu, and Houlu. The lawyer retained by Mrs. Ma was Xi Yafu. At the time of engagement, both parties entered into a contract stipulating that if the case was won, 30% of the recovered assets would be paid as legal fees. Subsequently, the case was settled out of court, and Mrs. Ma obtained 10,000 yuan. She notified Lawyer Xi and requested that the case be dismissed. Upon learning that the client had received 10,000 yuan, Lawyer Xi demanded 3,000 yuan in legal fees as per the contract. However, Mrs. Ma refused to pay and instead retained another lawyer, Lawyer Dan, who sent a letter to Lawyer Xi requesting that he not proceed further. Yesterday afternoon, the case was heard in the Eighth Tribunal. The judge, based on the requests of both parties, approved the withdrawal of the lawsuit. However, Lawyer Xi's legal fees remain unresolved. It is likely that further disputes will arise as Xi seeks to enforce the contract.

Three-Cent Stamps Used as One-Cent Stamps

Due to Excessive Stockpiles of Said Stamps

The Zilin Daily reports that recently, letters in Shanghai have often been seen with three-cent stamps affixed, bearing a "Temporarily Used as One Cent" stamp. Upon inquiring with Post Office Director Li Qi, it was learned that since the increase in postal rates for out-of-town mail from three cents to four cents on November 1, 1925, the post office has accumulated a considerable number of three-cent stamps that are not easily sold. Fearing that they will deteriorate over time and waste public funds, the postal authorities have ordered that they be stamped and used as one-cent stamps. This practice is not limited to the Shanghai area; it is being implemented nationwide.

Mother of Deceased Testifies About the Incident

After the incident, the deceased's mother, Song Gao, came to the factory and told me. That day at 1:00 PM, I asked for leave to search for them in the Gaolang Bridge area and the riverbank, fearing that she would commit suicide by drowning. But I found no trace of them. I also went to Suzhou to search, because Shunlin used to be a policeman in Suzhou. He and the deceased also met in Suzhou. They came to Shanghai together and lived in the back building of my house. I searched in Suzhou for two days, but did not find them. I had to return to Shanghai and saw the news that Song Qiaobao had been murdered by her lover, Shunlin, and her body was found under the bed. I was shocked and dared not go home, so I fled to Pudong. My brother Shungui, I don't know where he has fled to either. I have nothing to do with this case." Judge Ge ordered the defendant to pay a bail of 300 yuan and adjourned the case for further investigation and hearing.

Dumping Filth into Gutter

Watching the Alleyway Man Repeatedly Advised

Pan Zhigen Gathered Crowd to Commit Assault

Pan Zhigen runs the Xinxing Printing House on Guangxi Road, and his family also resides there. His wife is not concerned about hygiene, and secretly dumps excrement into the gutter outside the back door of the printing house. When dumping, the stench spreads everywhere, causing passersby to hold their noses. Especially with the pleasant spring weather, it is particularly harmful to hygiene. If it accumulates for a long time and clogs the gutter, the trouble will be even greater. Therefore, Luo Zuqiu, the alleyway watcher, repeatedly advised Pan's wife, but she turned a deaf ear. At noon on the 14th of this month, she dumped filth into the gutter again and Luo witnessed it and stepped out to stop her. However, Pan Zhigen also sided with his wife and gathered the printing workers he hired, including Xie Yingtang, to commit assault. Luo's eyes were both seriously injured, and his face was scratched, with fresh blood flowing. It was only stopped after the neighbors intervened and mediated. Luo was unwilling to be humiliated and hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Pan and his wife, as well as Xie Yingtang, in the Provisional Court for assault, and requested that in addition to being punished according to the law, they compensate for medical expenses and other losses. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang opened the court for trial. Only Pan's wife appeared in court. The plaintiff first stated the cause of the conflict and submitted the injury certificate issued by Renji Hospital to prove that he was indeed beaten by Pan and the others. Judge Wang then questioned Pan's wife, and her testimony was evasive. She then ordered a postponement to wait for Pan Zhigen and Xie Yingtang to be summoned to court for further questioning.

Appeal from Struck Fishing Boat

The Ningbo fishing boat Xinyulong, loaded with sand and gravel, was coming to Shanghai when it encountered the Nisshin Company's Japanese ship Yueyang Maru at the exit and was sunk. The boat owner, Yu Rugao, specially submitted a report to the Shipping Administration Bureau to negotiate with the company. The following is an excerpt from the report: "Report concerning boat being sunk, requesting that compensation be ordered in order to demonstrate justice and show compassion. This merchant owns the fishing boat Xinyulong, with a load capacity of 65 tons, which has been engaged in transporting goods such as sand, gravel, paper, and wood, without any accidents. On this occasion, the Xinyulong was loaded with a ship of yellow sand from Changtu, Dinghai, intending to sell it in Shanghai. At approximately 8:00 AM on March 24th, while traveling near the power plant, there was a southeasterly wind and rising tide.

Page 16

The Xinyulong was sailing along the Puxi port side when, due to the fog, the Yueyang Maru ship was exiting the port and struck the Xinyulong's port side due to the fog. The middle cabin immediately sank. The Yueyang Maru also knew that it had caused the accident and stopped for about an hour. The Xinyulong crew negotiated with the Yueyang Maru crew, who agreed to send someone to the Nisshin Company to settle the matter. The ship then exited the port. Now that the Xinyulong ship has sunk in the port, it is clearly a shallow water area, which is evidence of the Yueyang's mistake. As the sunken ship is in the port, there are many ships entering and exiting, which is very dangerous. It is requested that your office consider the difficult situation and quickly order the company to estimate the compensation and arrange for the Xinyulong sunken ship to be salvaged in order to demonstrate justice and avoid accidents. Most urgently submitted to the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau."

Changes to Electricity Supply Areas for Chinese-Owned Zhabei and Two Electrical Companies in Fahua and Pusong

Filed with the Construction Committee with the Approval of the Municipal Government

Previously, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau temporarily assigned the Fahua and Pusong districts to the business areas of the Chinese-owned Zhabei and two electrical companies, respectively. The south belongs to the Chinese-owned company, and the north belongs to Zhabei. The Municipal Government submitted it to the Construction Committee for review. Municipal Government Announces Regulations for the Management of Livestock Farms

The Municipal Health Bureau, in order to prevent hygiene hazards caused by those engaged in the poultry and livestock industry, had previously submitted and obtained approval from the municipal government to issue "Regulations for the Management of Poultry and Livestock Product Stores and Factories." Since their implementation, they have been effective. However, poultry and livestock also carry the risk of transmitting infectious diseases to humans. After investigating, the Bureau found that livestock farms within the city, which engage in raising livestock and poultry, are also closely related to public health. Therefore, these livestock farms should also be managed to prevent disease. As such, the Bureau specifically supplemented and revised the aforementioned regulations the other day, submitting them to the Mayor for review. It is now known that the Municipal Government will repeal the previous regulations and formulate "Regulations for the Management of Livestock Farms and Poultry and Livestock Product Stores and Factories," which have already been announced. The text is recorded as follows: Article 1: "Livestock farm" refers to places where various types of poultry and livestock are raised. "Poultry and livestock products" refers to items such as feathers, hides, bones, meat, eggs, milk, intestines, blood, oil, and residue of domestic and wild poultry and livestock, whether processed or unprocessed. All those engaged in these matters must comply with these regulations. Article 2: Anyone establishing a livestock farm or poultry and livestock product store or factory within this special municipality to engage in the business of poultry, livestock, or their products must apply to the Health Bureau for registration and obtain a business license. Those who do not comply with these regulations to apply for registration will not be allowed to operate. Article 3: When applying for registration, livestock farms or poultry and livestock product stores and factories must report the following items: (1) Name and detailed address of the livestock farm or store/factory engaged in business. (2) Date of establishment. (3) Type of poultry and livestock raised or type of poultry and livestock products sold. (4) Whether the business premises' buildings and land are owned or leased; if leased, the start and expiration dates of the lease must be stated. (5) Average number of poultry and livestock produced annually, or the average number of products produced, stored, manufactured, or sold monthly. Article 4: Livestock farms or poultry and livestock product stores and factories must comply with all hygiene regulations of this special municipality. Article 5: Livestock farms or poultry and livestock product stores and factories must apply for registration once every year in January and pay a license fee of one silver dollar. Those who do not comply with these regulations to apply for registration will have their operations suspended. Article 6: Livestock farms or poultry and livestock product stores and factories must post the registration certificate issued by the Health Bureau in a conspicuous place for public viewing. Article 7: If the registration certificate is lost, the Health Bureau may be petitioned for a replacement, but the license fee must be paid again according to the regulations, and a public notice must be placed in the newspaper in advance. Article 8: Livestock farms or poultry and livestock product stores and factories must not be located in dirty or noisy areas. Each store and factory opened before the promulgation of these regulations may be guided to improve or be ordered to relocate by the Health and Civil Affairs Bureau at any time. Article 9: The buildings and all equipment of livestock farms and poultry and livestock product stores and factories must be cleaned and maintained at all times to emphasize public health. Article 10: These regulations may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 11: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation by the Special Municipal Government.

A Little Lioness Deceived in a Love Affair

Cai Jiaqing Entices and Abducts

A woman from Bao Ying named Little Lioness, who is seventeen years old, has been working in the rough yarn section of a certain Japanese-owned yarn factory near Little Sand Ferry for two years. She resides in the workshop of her fellow villager Cui Shen, where she earns over four corners of wages each day. Over the past two years, she has accumulated fifty dollars in wages. A labor strike recently occurred at the yarn factory, and Little Lioness has been at home without work. She carried over twenty dollars, planning to go to the Chi Bang Bridge on Carter Road to buy clothes. On the way, she met Cai Jiaqing (nicknamed Jiaqingzi), a man who is known to be a loafer in the Little Sand Ferry area. Cai is twenty years old and from Dongtai. Little Lioness, not knowing the way, asked Cai for directions. Cai saw an opportunity and volunteered to guide her, asking her to take the tram with him. Unexpectedly, he lured her to a small inn near East New Bridge. He enticed her in every way, and Little Lioness, lacking knowledge, was raped. They stayed at the inn for four nights, and all her twenty dollars were swindled away by Cai. Yesterday morning, while Little Lioness was asleep, Cai took advantage of the situation and stole Little Lioness's new silk satin padded jacket and pants and fled without a trace. When Little Lioness woke up, the man was gone, and her padded jacket and pants were also missing. Realizing she had been deceived, she cried loudly in the room. Later, the waiter entered and asked about the situation, and demanded the two nights of rent owed, totaling ten corners. Little Lioness, having no way, begged the waiter to go to Little Sand Ferry and summon her landlady Cui Shen, who paid the rent and took her away in a rickshaw.

Husband and Wife Accuse Each Other of Attempted Murder

A woman from Yancheng, Hong Zhou, yesterday accused her husband, Hong Xiangshan, of plotting to murder her at the Fourth District Headquarters. According to Zhou's testimony, she is twenty-eight years old and lives in Fumei Lane, Haichang Road. She and Hong have been married for several years and were considered harmonious. Unexpectedly, he recently neglected his duty to provide for her and often abused her. The other day, she fled to her mother's house to avoid him. Yesterday, she went back and he suddenly confined her in a room, denying her food and drink. At night, while she was sleeping, he took a leather knife, intending to chop her head. Fortunately, she woke up in alarm and hurriedly left the bed, avoiding the murder. But her husband's intentions are treacherous, and it is difficult to live with him, so she reported to the headquarters to investigate. Hong Xiangshan testified that he is twenty-six years old and a leatherworker. He has always treated his wife well. However, starting this year, she often went back to her parents' home. When he tried to dissuade her, she did not return for several days. He secretly investigated and learned that she had a new lover. But he knew he was poor and that it was not easy to marry a wife, so he swallowed his anger and brought her back. Who knew that she would be so aggressive and would try to strangle him with a large rope while he was sleeping. Fortunately, he noticed it early and took a leather knife to scare her. Unexpectedly, she falsely accused him of attempted murder. Director Jin reviewed the testimonies and, considering the case involved a criminal matter and the testimonies conflicted, ordered that they both be sent to the bureau for interrogation.

Li Commits Suicide by Swallowing Match Heads

Why Did Xu Jinchen Flee?

Xu Jinchen, a man from Danyang who runs a beef shop at No. 188 Huiwen Road, Zhabei, is twenty-five years old. His business has not been very prosperous, and his wife, Li, who is twenty-one years old and from Yangzhong, have a poor relationship and often quarrel. The other day, they argued again over trivial matters, which led to physical violence. Li, filled with resentment and lamenting her unfortunate fate, felt that life was not worth living. She secretly bought several boxes of "Black Head" matches, cut off the heads, and swallowed them with liquor. At nine o'clock that night, she was poisoned and rolled around on the bed. Xu, realizing she had taken poison, sent her to Jishi Hospital for treatment, but it was too late, and she died. Xu, fearing punishment, fled. The police have been notified and have reported to the local court to send someone for examination.

They requested permission to dispatch detectives to assist in the arrest. The head of the detectives approved and immediately ordered detectives to assist in arresting Zhu and Jiang. They were arrested and yesterday sent to the French Court for interrogation. First, the visiting detective stated the case and requested extradition. After a brief interrogation of the two defendants by Chinese and Western officials, the court granted permission to hand over the two defendants to the visiting detective to be taken back for trial.

Suing for Illegal Sale of Company and Assault

Wang Hou'an, a man from Sichuan, retained a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the French Court, stating that the plaintiff and Wang Boqin, Wang Kuilü, Wang Hongbin, Ye Huasheng, etc., jointly established the Chuan Yu Company on Avenue Edward VII. Unexpectedly, last year, the defendant Wang Boqin and others privately sold the company to Qiu Dongrong. In reality, Wang Boqin bought it himself, secretly colluding with Qiu Dongrong as the buyer. After the plaintiff discovered this and made accusations, they ignored him. The defendants are guilty of embezzlement. Also, last winter, the defendant Yu Boqin beat the plaintiff's daughter for no reason and kicked her, causing injuries. There is a Western doctor's certificate to prove this, which constitutes the crime of assault. He requested the court to investigate. The defendant, Wang Boqin, retained lawyer Fei Xizhen to defend, stating that the plaintiff's accusation of assault is without definite evidence and the regulations cited by the plaintiff's lawyer cannot be established. As for the business dispute, it is a civil matter, and the plaintiff had already acknowledged the sale at the time, for which there is evidence to prove. How can he go back on his word? He requested that the plaintiff's accusation be dismissed. Wang Kuilü, Wang Hongbin, and others retained lawyers to make a defense. Qiu Dongrong also retained lawyer Ba Yun to defend, saying that his client invested in buying the business through legitimate procedures and the plaintiff should not be involved for no reason. He requested that the plaintiff be severely punished. Chinese and Western officials reviewed the testimonies and declared the debate concluded, to be decided later.

Car Crash Causes Wall to Collapse, Killing a Person

Wang Jinxian, a twenty-year-old construction worker from Jiangbei, lived at No. 175 Sanguantang, Xieqiao. On the 24th, at the doorway of the wall west of the French Concession Police Station on Rue Massenet, a cargo truck No. 752 driven by Zhang Haitian, a driver from the French Public Works Bureau, was driving by. For some reason, the front of the truck went onto the sidewalk, causing the wall to collapse, crushing Wang's head, causing profuse bleeding. The police arrived, recorded the license plate number, and sent the injured person to Guangci Hospital for treatment. They also reported back to the head of the detectives for review. Wang died of his injuries shortly after being admitted to the hospital. The hospital notified the police, who had the body taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall mortuary for examination. The police ordered detectives to notify the deceased's father, Wang Yushan, and witnesses Bai Hongsheng and Xu Sandi to come to the station. Yesterday morning, Mr. Zhu, the judge from the Vehicle Affairs Department of the French Court, arrived at the mortuary at 11:00 AM and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died from injuries sustained in a car accident. Because the deceased's family was poor, he ordered Tongren Fuyuan Hall to provide a coffin and burial and await submission to the court for review.

Autopsy of a Male Corpse in a Cemetery Confirms Death from Illness

An unidentified male corpse was found in the Jinjiaqiao Cemetery in Yangjingbei, Pudong, the other day. The local security reported it to the local court for autopsy. Upon instructions, the corpse was taken to the court for examination. Yesterday morning, the local security took the corpse to the court, where prosecutor Yang and two autopsy examiners, Shen Xuan, etc., arrived at the scene. The corpse was found to be about fifty years old, with a mustache, wearing a melon-shaped hat, a fake Zhigong woolen padded robe, black cotton-padded jacket and pants, a striped cloth shirt, and a sanitary undershirt. However, the words "Ding Jiyu" were written on all of his clothes. There was a three-button wallet beside him, with the words "Chinese Public School University Department Ding Shunxing Laundry Service." There were no injuries on his body, and he had died from illness. It was certain that this person was Ding Jiyu of Ding Shunxing, but it is puzzling why he died in the Jinjiaqiao Cemetery, which is ten miles north of Yangjing. The body has now been photographed and taken into custody by the court to await identification by relatives.

Questions About the Fire in the Warehouse

If No One Went In or Out, Where Did the Fire Come From?

A man surnamed Deng from Pudong, who runs Juyu Yarn Shop at No. 115 Wangjia Wharf, Nanshi, has his family living separately at No. 2 Yong'an Lane, Dongjiadu. Deng, because the goods in the shop have recently become crowded and insufficient for storage, set aside another room in his home to store yarn goods and forbade idlers from entering. Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, a fire suddenly broke out in the warehouse room. In an instant, smoke filled the air, and the flames blazed, making it impossible to approach. Soon after, the fire brigades from various districts learned of the fire and immediately drove to the scene to put it out, which they were able to do quickly. Afterwards, the patrol police from the area took Deng's shop assistant back to the First Section of the First District. The section chief preliminarily interrogated the assistant. Because the room only contained goods and no one went in or out, where did the fire start? Moreover, it was found that he had insured the fire for over three thousand taels. Therefore, there are many suspicious points about the cause of this fire. He immediately ordered a written report to be submitted to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

China Foreign Famine Relief Committee – Report on the Disaster in Northern Jiangsu

The China Foreign Famine Relief Committee received an investigative report from Wang Shaohan, the President of the Bao Ying, China, and Anglican Church, and Pastor Meng Gemei, stating that on the 7th of this month, Han and Pastor Meng went to the disaster area to examine the households in detail. Even the grain eaten by chickens and dogs and the food consumed by rats are gone. The disaster victims eat water plants and wheat bran, which they cook and swallow. Tofu dregs and dried sweet potatoes are considered supreme delicacies. The feces in the latrines are no different from pig manure, indicating that there is no food in their stomachs. They cannot speak audibly, and they walk unsteadily, on the verge of collapse. They are barely alive and may not last until the next day. It is unbearable to look at them. Some have hanged themselves because they have no food to feed their children. Families are crying, and even the most hardened person would shed tears. The corpses of those who have starved to death in the makeshift shelters in the burial grounds are piled up everywhere. Alas, the dead are gone, but how will the surviving disaster victims be saved? The above is only what we saw in the villages thirty miles from the city. It is said that twenty or thirty miles further east, the disaster is even more severe than what we saw. We urge you to quickly grant a relief fund of at least ten thousand yuan to save the imminent needs of tens of thousands of lives. In addition, the famine victims' representatives from Xinghua County, the township head of Shangjiao Township, Shu Jiashu, and others, sent a letter stating that the disaster situation in their area is extremely tragic. Countless strong men have fled to other places. The elderly, weak, women, and children are unable to move and have nowhere to beg, so they eat grass roots and tree bark to fill their stomachs, causing many to have swollen faces. From winter to spring, countless people have died. The refugees will soon return, and there will be even more people without food. The disaster is unimaginable. Therefore, we have no choice but to urgently plead for you to quickly release relief funds to save the disaster victims.

Zhejiang Provincial Private Electricity Industry Federation Executive and Supervisory Committee

Meeting Held in Shanghai Yesterday

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the Zhejiang Provincial Private Electricity Industry Federation held its third joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees at No. 11 Jiujiang Road. Representatives present included Jiang Tiaosheng from Jinhua, Ye Yangwu from Shaoxing, Yang Bo'an from Jiaxing, Shen Sifang from Wuxing, Han Yimin from Pinghu, Zhang Zhiyi from Jiashan, Cheng Jian from Lanxi, Sun Luren from Xin Chongde, and Gao Leqin from Changxing. Those attending as observers included Zhong Huibo and Zhong Lansun. Ye Yangwu chaired the meeting, reported on the approximate accounts for the 18th year, and Shen Sifang reported on the results of the previous year's petition and the recent situation of the general association. Matters for discussion: (1) How should this association bear the general association's membership fee? It was resolved that members of this association, in addition to having already joined the general association, should extract a certain percentage from the membership fees paid to this association by other companies as the general association's membership fee. At the same time, members will be given the qualifications to submit proposals when standing committee members attend the general association. (2) How should the undertakings organized under Article 3 of the articles of association be implemented? It was resolved to vigorously promote this article to the industry through communication. (3) Should membership fees be appropriately reduced for colleagues with smaller power generation capacity? It was resolved that hereafter, when colleagues join the association, those with a power generation capacity below fifty kilowatts should have their monthly fees reduced to two yuan, and those with less than ten kilowatts should have their fees reduced to one yuan. (4) The date for the next meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees was decided. It will be held in Shanghai on June 8th (Sunday). (5) Organizing an electrical industry consumer cooperative and promoting domestic goods. It was resolved to first investigate the electrical material consumption situation of each industry colleague and encourage the adoption of domestic goods.

Radio Telegraph Operator on Probation

Examination Regulations Have Been Announced

The "Regulations for the Examination of Radio Telegraph Operators on Probation" drafted by the Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications have been approved and promulgated. The regulations are recorded below: (1) Anyone who is over sixteen years of age, in good health, of good character, fluent in Chinese and English, has graduated from a radio school or other school of equivalent level, and possesses the level stipulated in Article 2 may take the radio telegraph operator on probation examination. (2) Applicants must have the following knowledge and skills: (A) Ability to send and receive Chinese and English code at an average speed of at least sixteen words per minute (each word consists of five letters, numbers, or symbols). (B) Basic radio theory and practical knowledge of repair. (C) Communication rules, response methods, and telegraphy abbreviations. (3) The examination subjects are: 1. Party Principles, 2. Chinese, 3. English, 4. Radio Transmission and Reception, 5. Radio Theory, 6. Communication Procedures, 7. Overview of Business Rules. (4) For the grades of each subject, except for Radio Transmission and Reception, which must be at least 80 points, the other subjects are calculated as a percentage. An overall percentage of 60 or above is considered passing. The percentages are described on the left: (1) Party Principles 14%, (2) Chinese 15%, (3) English 15%, (4) Radio Theory 18%, (5) Communication Procedures 20%, (6) Overview of Business Rules 18%. (5) Anyone who possesses the qualifications in Article 2 and passes the examination by the Radio Administration may become a radio telegraph operator on probation, assigned to various stations for probation, and reported to the Ministry by the Radio Administration for record. (6) Radio telegraph operators on probation who pass the examination may be given the treatment of the elementary class of the Ministry's Telecommunications School and be assigned to stations for a three-month probation period, with a monthly allowance of 16 yuan. After the probation period, the managing engineer or engineer of each station will assess them. Those with excellent performance will be removed from probation and given a minimum salary of 32 yuan in accordance with Articles 17 and 19 of the Radio Telegraph Operator Regulations. Those with average performance will be dismissed. (7) The examination and employment of these radio operators should be determined by the Radio Administration when the radio stations are short of personnel. The Radio Administration will determine the number of positions and report it to the Ministry for approval before recruiting. The date and location of the examination will be determined and notified by the Radio Administration on a temporary basis. (8) All applicants must present a graduation diploma and submit a four-inch half-length photo and a registration fee of one yuan at the time of registration. Regardless of whether they pass or fail, the registration fee and photo will not be returned. (9) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended and submitted to the Ministry at any time. (10) These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation. It is said that the Radio Administration will not be recruiting this type of personnel in the near future. If there is a recruitment, the Radio Administration will announce the number of positions and the date in the newspaper.

Guangdong Aviation Students Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday

Heading to Beijing Soon

Sixteen graduates from the third graduating class of the Guangdong Aviation School, under the order of Director Zhang of the Aviation Administration, have been transferred to Beijing to serve. It is reported that these students arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong yesterday. After a short rest, they will proceed to Beijing.

Lost Guangdong Girl Awaiting Pickup

A few days ago, a Guangdong girl named Deng Peilan, aged eleven, wearing blue cotton clothes, got lost in the French Concession. A police officer found her and took her to the police station. After finding no family members, she was sent to the French Court yesterday for instructions. The court ordered her to be sent to the orphanage to await family members to claim her.

Records of Robberies and Thefts

Rue du Père Huc: At 7:30 PM last night, three robbers broke into house number 21, Lane 8 on Rue du Père Huc. Two robbers were armed with guns, ordering silence. They stole clothing and silver dollars worth 100 yuan before fleeing.

Route Massenet: At around 8 PM last night, three robbers suddenly arrived at house number 6, Mingde Lane, Route Massenet in the French Concession. Two robbers, armed with guns, ransacked the house upstairs and downstairs. It is estimated that clothing and cash worth over 100 yuan were stolen before they fled. The victim reported the incident to the police for investigation.

Active Reorganization of Silk and Satin Dyeing Prices

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Industry Labor-Management Joint Reorganization Dyeing Price Committee held a citywide manager meeting at the Nine Mu Di meeting hall yesterday. All members were present. Many important matters were resolved, including: (1) Dyeing bills for March: It was publicly decided that all collections would be handled by the Reorganization Committee. (2) A small number of silk shops had not paid their dyeing bills for the previous month. It was publicly decided to file lawsuits with the local court and order all dyeing factories in the city to stop accepting goods from them. Any unauthorized dyeing would be severely punished upon discovery, and rewards would be offered. (3) Unification of dyeing factories using the Heji brand: It was publicly decided that no attached brands would be allowed, and those that existed would be immediately canceled. (4) Placement of unemployed workers: Over ten people were selected on the spot to serve in various dyeing factories as supervisors. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Six Organizations Commemorate Mrs. Li Huang

Six organizations, including the Shanghai South Qingxin Church, the Boys' and Girls' School, and Pu Yi Du, held a meeting at the church the other day to commemorate Mrs. Huang, the wife of Li Hengchun, who contributed the most to the establishment of the new church. Jiang Shixu chaired the meeting. Ms. Ding Xiang performed a solo of mournful music. Mrs. Guo Bingwen recounted her life story. The Bible College and the church choir sang mourning hymns. Mr. Chen and Mr. Wang gave speeches. Mr. Chen Chunsheng and others delivered eulogies. Li Hengchun gave a thank-you speech at the end. More than 300 male and female guests attended. After the meeting, tea and snacks were served, and the meeting adjourned.

Wake Held for Lawyer Xu Shichang's Mother

Mrs. Wang, the mother of lawyer Xu Wuchang, passed away last month. Yesterday, a wake was held at the Guandi Temple in Laoximen. Attendees were mostly from the military and political circles. Former Premier Sun Baoqi inscribed a memorial, and female students from the Liangjiang Girls' Physical Education School sang mourning songs, creating a grand event.

Death of Dr. Xie Boli, Female Physician

Dr. Xie Boli, an American female physician and director of the Bao Ying Hospital on Linping Road in Hongkou, was kind-hearted and diligent. For four years, the local common people benefited greatly from her services. Her work was an urgent necessity for the local area. Dr. Xie, knowing her age, continued to serve the public despite illness. She fell ill last month and was admitted to the Bo Bei Li Hospital, where she never recovered. She passed away last Saturday afternoon. Colleagues from the Tongren Hospital, including Mr. and Mrs. Diao Xinde, Mr. and Mrs. Bode from the Renji Hospital, Dr. Wu Jingyao, Zheng Zeng Enxi, and Weng Guoxun, sent her body to the Universal Funeral Home at 71 Jiaozhou Road for a temporary resting place. It was then decided that Diao Xinde, a member of the hospital board, would continue the hospital affairs, Weng Guodong would preside over the school affairs, and Liu Liqian would assist with all matters.

Record of the Spring Meeting of the Martial Arts Association

After Zhu Guofu, the general director of the Shanghai Martial Arts Association, was appointed as the director of education at the Central Guoshu (National Martial Arts) Institute, the association's affairs continued. Yesterday, a spring meeting was held at the first meeting hall on Xizang Road to develop the association's affairs. Twenty-one people attended. The ceremony began at 3:00 PM. The ceremony was conducted according to the proper etiquette. First, the director of general affairs, Weng Guoxun, presided over the meeting, reporting on the progress of the association. Ling Ziguang, Wu Huichuan, Zhang Changyi, and others expressed their opinions, all strongly supporting continued efforts to achieve the initial goal of strengthening the body and strengthening the country. It was then decided to invite Zhao Daoxin, Zhang Changxin, and Wang Deyuan as professors, and Xie Zhili as the resident host. The entrance fee within six months is six yuan for ordinary members and ten yuan for special members. Classes are held from 6:00 to 8:00 AM and from 8:00 to 10:00 PM. Members can also practice at the association at any time and study with each other.

Recent News from the World Moral Society

Jin Shuren, chairman of the Xinjiang Provincial Government, wrote to Xu Yabo, chairman of the World Moral Society, yesterday, saying: "Your establishment of the World Moral Society, uniting Chinese and foreign comrades to address current ills, is commendable at a time when people are deceitful and morals are declining. If no one steps forward to remedy this, we will see the collapse of embankments and the decline of rivers, and the fall of morality to what end? Your society advocates for the respect of etiquette and loudly calls for the reversal of the decline, the encouragement of good deeds in the future, the awakening of the deaf, and the support of the world and the manifestation of education. I deeply admire your elegant planning. I have written an inscription for your review and preservation. I hope that you will receive and keep it. This is my sincere hope."

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that a low-pressure area was forming in the Sichuan area, and another low-pressure area in the Pacific Ocean was moving from the south towards the Ogasawara Islands. The weather here is warm and clear. The wind along the coast of the country is gentle and extremely unstable, and there is fog. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the port was 74.8 degrees and the lowest was 49.6 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 60.4 degrees and the lowest was 49.5 degrees.
