Free Talk

Laughing It Off

— Sea Traveler

A: Your wife is someone I know.

B: One day, I was driving my car in the city and accidentally hit her. The police arrived and took me to court. The court ordered me to pay 10,000 gold in damages. I thought it would be cheaper to marry her.

A: Why are you so listless today, not happy at all?

B: My wife ran away yesterday.

A: If I were in your position, I wouldn't care. I would feel much lighter.

B: I was originally happy too. Who knew she would come back again this morning?

A: You once had two different views on gambling, one moral and one immoral. How do you distinguish them?

B: That's very simple. When you participate in a gambling game, if you win big, then gambling is moral. If you lose, then gambling is immoral.

A: When can you pay me back the money you owe me?

B: Your question reminds me of what happened to my son in school.

A: What happened?

B: That hateful teacher asked him a difficult question that he couldn't answer.

A Record of the Panic Regarding the Holy Mother Statue in Rome

— Qiu Shui

Since Soviet Russia implemented the anti-religious movement, the killing of priests and the destruction of churches in the country have been reported daily in the newspapers. It is not necessary to elaborate further. Even abroad, the Soviet Russian Communist Party is planning to destroy Christianity. Recently, Western newspapers published a communication from London on the 15th, stating that a large number of secret Soviet Russian groups have arrived in Rome to engage in anti-religious work. Because Rome is the residence of the Pope and the center of global Christianity. The Soviet Russian Communist Party started with its center, which can be said to be cunning. After the secret Soviet Russian group arrived in Rome, their first demonstration was to destroy the statue of the Virgin Mary in the Vatican Gardens in Rome's Wantie Kaihua Garden. The statue was established by Pope Alexander III. It has a long history and is a huge project. Not only is it carefully maintained and worshiped by people in the church, but even visitors from afar cannot help but look up and admire it when they pass by. The Roman church was extremely panicked after hearing that the secret Soviet Russian group had arrived, and they gathered to discuss protection measures. But after a long time, nothing was heard. However, nearby residents have since heard the sound of a pack of dogs barking wildly under the statue late at night. The sound is sharp and long, as if there were bandits approaching the door, and giant mastiffs were rising up to resist. So the people told each other that the Pope had recently raised fierce mastiffs to protect the Holy Mother. Although the Soviet Russian Communist Party is violent, they will also encounter setbacks. Those who are superstitious about the way of God even said that the Holy Mother showed her spirit to resist the violent. That is even more ridiculous. I do not know that there is no dog next to the statue of the Holy Mother. The barking sound at night is a secret mechanism, not that there are hundreds of giant mastiffs to protect this statue. The church people have discussed good plans for protecting the statue, as mentioned above. Among them, there is a priest named Father Lulgi Marmagg, an expert in wireless electricity who has ingenuity. First, he provided a wonderful mechanism. The method is to connect the gramophone record of the sound of dog barking with electricity, install a speaker, and secretly place it on the right side of the statue, and then connect the yin and yang wires to the statue's surroundings. A trigger is set up separately. If an uninvited guest approaches the statue, the foot touches the trigger, the yin and yang electricity are connected, and the gramophone starts automatically, communicating the sound to the speaker. So the sound is as loud as the barking of a pack of dogs. The installation of this machine was very secret beforehand. Only the priest and his assistant knew about it. Therefore, on the second day after the machine was completed, the Pope happened to be touring the area, and his foot suddenly touched the secret machine. In an instant, the dogs barked wildly, as if they were about to pounce and devour him. The Pope was shocked and immediately avoided him, ordering the guards to patrol, but he found nothing. The priest told him about it, and they all laughed. It is also an interesting event. According to history, this kind of machine is not a new invention. The most famous one is the palace of the ancient Emperor Solomon, where there were fake lions roaring to protect the royal chamber. Khan of the ancient Byzantine also set up a mechanism. Whenever foreign envoys paid homage to the palace and approached the throne, there was the sound of lions roaring to surprise foreigners. Today's Roman priests are just imitating his method. Only the skill of its machinery should far exceed that of ancient times. It can be asserted.

A Small Robbery in Bailuzhou

— Wei

There are quite a few famous scenic spots in the capital. Bailuzhou is also one of them. It is located in the southeast of the city. You can reach it after a few hundred steps across the Qinhuai River. Although it is not very secluded, it also has a charming garden and fresh air. It is rare to find this area full of singing and music. Moreover, it also has the famous line of the poet saint Li Bai, "The two waters divide Bailuzhou." Unfortunately, the army was stationed here last year. The pavilions, trees, and plants were severely damaged. Stones were stacked to make stoves, and bricks were piled up to make toilets. Cooking here, urinating here. Bailuzhou in the area has become a camp. Recently, when I went there, although the stationed people have moved away, the glorious notice of protection from the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs has been posted. But it is still full of desolation and the relics have not been completely removed.

The Mystery of the Barbershop

— Yan Ye

Any barbershop always has two cylindrical things of about two feet long and the size of a bowl as a trademark in front of their doors. Red, black, and white colors are painted on them, spiraling upwards, like three belts. Electricity runs through the middle, making them spin endlessly. At night, electric lights are installed inside, making them spin really interestingly. People in the countryside are often attracted to stop and watch when they first come to Shanghai. Some, even if they don't use this cylindrical spinning thing, will definitely paint the same two on the flat surface in front of the door. I have long suspected this thing. Why is it necessary to use this thing as a trademark? I asked many people, but they didn't understand. Sometimes they even asked me instead. Later I thought that the barbers themselves would eventually know. I didn't know that when I had a haircut, I asked five or six shops, but they all didn't know why. They just said that it was an old trademark passed down for many years. People who have returned from abroad say that the trademarks of barbershops in all countries of the world are also this thing. So I concluded that this trademark must be universal, and its origin must be abroad. Recently, I asked someone who is familiar with foreign stories, but he still didn't dare to say for sure. He said that he heard that there was a surgeon in Europe in the past. He used this spiraling thing as his trademark. Because amputations and broken feet require bandages, the three colors on the pillar are the pictographic representation of bandages. Later, he abandoned his benevolent medical practice and became a barber, who worked on the top of the head. But although he changed his profession, he did not change his trademark. Each barbershop found his logo to be interesting, so they unconsciously imitated it. It has only been spread to various countries until now. After he finished speaking, he solemnly said, "I really dare not decide whether this explanation is true or false." Then this mystery still cannot be revealed.

The Swan of the Library

— Xiao Peng

The swan is a water bird. It is also known as the swan. It always lives in lakes and swamps. It is not often seen daily. A swan was obtained by the Public Library of this county (Tongshan) the other day. It was given by Liu Buzhou, a person from the county. It turned out that on a certain night in the first ten days of the first lunar month of this year, when Liu was in a deep sleep, he heard the sound of rustling in the yard. Suspecting that there was a thief, he got up, dressed, and lit a candle. But the door was still the same. There were no burglars. Later, he saw an object in the corner of the yard. Seeing that it was completely white, neither a crane nor a goose, he was surprised by it. So he tied it in the courtyard. Later, someone came to see it and recognized it as a swan. Liu felt that it was a waste to raise it in his home, so it was better to put it in a public place for public viewing. Therefore, he donated it to the library. The swan is larger than a goose. Its feathers are white and glossy. Its beak is flat with a black front end. Its legs are short. Its feet are webbed. Looking at it, you know it is a waterfowl. Now the curator, Li, has built a wire cage field on the vacant space in the library. A pool is built inside, and a wooden house is connected next to it for the bird to swim and rest. Every day, people come to see it in an endless stream. They all say that the swan's arrival here is no less than a person falling behind. Red Velvet

Spring Opera News

Since the beginning of spring, famous actors in Pingzhong have been competing to perform new songs. It is heard that it can be performed in the shortest time.

It was scheduled to perform Yutangchun on the 14th, 15th, and 16th for three evenings. The play was also arranged as The Shadow of Candles and the Red Fur Lady. The third day happened to be Sunday, so Famen Temple was added to the performance in the daytime. It was heard that after the performance, he would return to Ping and perform with the Minghe Society at Hualeyuan. It is said that it will be necessary to wait for Guan Dayuan to return from Shanghai before a date can be chosen for the performance.

He Tuna Study

— Juemi

Every early spring, when river pufferfish emerge, there are incessant reports in newspapers of people dying from eating them. The name "river pufferfish" is not consistent, and their shapes probably vary as well. Therefore, I am writing a "He Tuna Study" and submitting it to this journal.

"Trust extends even to piglets and fish" is found in the Book of Changes. The name "river pufferfish" has been around for a long time. Zhuangzi once saw Zi eating his dead mother, and the piglet was sometimes written as 㹠. The Erya dictionary says that "鯸鮔" is the "魨." It has a green back and white belly, and it gets angry when touched. Its liver is deadly. The "鯸鮔" mentioned in Erya is likely the river pufferfish. The "Compendium of Materia Medica" says that the "魨" looks like a tadpole, with the larger ones being over a foot long. Their backs are greenish-white with yellow streaks and no scales. Their gills and eyes can puff up, and they are poisonous. It is also called "鯸鮧," "鰗鮧," and "䲅魚," originally written as "豚." The "魨" mentioned in the "Compendium of Materia Medica" is also the river pufferfish. The "Classic of Mountains and Seas" says that the Dun River flows eastward into the waters of Yanmen, and there are many "䰽" fish in it. Eating the "䰽" fish is deadly. The "Compendium of Materia Medica" says that this is the "鯸鯃." Therefore, the "䰽" fish mentioned in the "Classic of Mountains and Seas" is also the river pufferfish. Zuo Si's "Rhapsody on the Wu Capital" mentions "𩵭, tuna, and 鯸鮐." The commentary says that "鯸鮐" looks like a tadpole, with the larger ones being over a foot long. The belly is white, and the back is bluish-black with yellow patterns. This is exactly the same as the description of "鯸鮔" in Erya. Therefore, the "鯸鮐" mentioned in Zuo Si's "Rhapsody on the Wu Capital" is also the river pufferfish. Wang Chong's "Discourses Weighed in the Balance" says that salmon liver is deadly. Lei Gong's "Treatise on Preparing Herbs" says that salmon is also called "䲅魚" or "嗔魚." Rihua Zi calls it "鰗魚," and today it is called "river pufferfish." The "Compendium of Materia Medica" says that "䲅魚" is also called "鰗鮧." When touched, it gets angry and puffs up its belly like a balloon, hence the name "嗔魚." It has a white back with a red line like a seal. Its eyes can close, unlike other fish, and this is the river pufferfish of today. Therefore, the salmon and "䲅魚" mentioned in "Discourses Weighed in the Balance" and the "Compendium of Materia Medica" are also the river pufferfish. It can be known that "鯸鮐," "河魨," "䰽魚," "鯸鮐," "鮭魚," and "䲅魚" are all names for the river pufferfish, and "鯸鮧," "鰗鮧," and "嗔魚," etc., are all alternative names for the river pufferfish. The poison of the river pufferfish, as recorded in various books, is all in the liver. This is something that anyone who eats river pufferfish must know.

Paper Kite Talk

— Yang Yixiao

Gongshu carved a wooden kite that flew high. At that time, there were only kites and no paper kites. Later, when Hou Jing besieged Taicheng, Emperor Jianwen made a paper kite to send an urgent message to the outside world. This was the beginning of paper kites. During the Five Dynasties, Li Ye of the Han Dynasty and Emperor Yin made paper kites outside the palace and flew them. The "Record of Diverse Matters" says that today's paper kites are flown with strings, and children watch with open mouths, which can release internal heat. Who would have known that paper kites would be transmitted abroad? The great American scholar Benjamin Franklin invented aerial electricity because of them. Today, the research on paper kites in the West is making rapid progress, especially in England. There are paper kite competitions, which are extremely popular.

Warmth on My Heart (156)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: Fiery Flames Light Up the Pavilion, Filial Daughter Admired; Red Carpet Laid Out, Famous Actors Met

That Weichun Garden is rented out to people for meetings. You just need to negotiate with the garden owner a few days in advance, and if you offer a reasonable rental price, he will agree. However, when there are intense meetings, he often doesn't get what he deserves. Why is that? Those meetings are all for public benefit, so the daily rental price requires him to help out, and he can't ask for too much. When the meeting is in progress, anyone can come, because it's open to the public. They crowd his big Western-style house, called Andy, until it's packed like sardines. Some people are squeezed in the back and can't see who the speaker is, so they step on the chairs and tables, breaking the chairs. With so many people talking at once, who can you ask to pay for the damages? I remember one time, for the sake of some Russian volunteer team, a national assembly was held in Zhang's Garden. At that time, the spirit of the Chinese people was being stirred up. It was said that the meeting would start at 2 o'clock, but by 1 o'clock, it was already packed. Several patriots had just returned from Japan. Like the current senior statesman of the party-state, Mr. Wu Zhihui, he had also just returned from Japan. Today, he would be giving a speech, and even more people came. He gave a very passionate speech, and at the most emphatic point, he would punch the table. By the end, his voice was hoarse and his fist was swollen, but he had also broken the mahogany table. After this meeting, after everyone had left, the garden owner inspected the equipment. Thirteen chairs were broken, one mahogany Eight Immortals table was smashed, and more than a dozen teapots and teacups were broken. Who could he ask for compensation? He could only admit his bad luck. However, Zhang's Garden, because meetings were always held there, has a very memorable record in history. Some of the current great figures of the party-state still remember it. Moreover, meetings are always held on Sundays, and Sundays are the busiest days in Zhang's Garden. The foreign clerks and the "masters" from the brothels also come to Zhang's Garden on this day to ride around in horse-drawn carriages. Zhang's Garden has a road built in a circle, so you can go from the east side to the west side. Therefore, those dissipated playboys and enchanting beauties, famous courtesans and national scholars are often crowded together. Fortunately, that Weichun Garden is inclusive and does not discriminate. There are elegant events and vulgar events. There are orchid shows, chrysanthemum shows, and on good days in spring and autumn, many people gather to compose poems on assigned topics and form poetry societies. That can be considered an elegant event. However, there are also often instances of adulterous grooms and actors, and dirty pimps fighting over jealousy. They would make appointments with gangsters, and each would call on their own henchmen, bringing iron rulers and knives, and fight it out. These kinds of things often happened in Zhang's Garden. This can be considered extremely vulgar, but it's not a big deal in Shanghai.

The market situation was relatively stable, with only two or three mace (a unit of weight) fluctuations in the forward and backward markets. Grain: Rice Market Sees Repeated Price Increases

Top Grade Japonica Rice Already Called at 21 Yuan

Zhabei: Yesterday, the supply of goods coming down the river became increasingly scarce, and inventory continued to deplete. Therefore, buyers became increasingly eager to purchase, and sellers inevitably raised prices to sell. As a result, top-grade white Japonica rice was even quoted at 21 yuan. Ultimately, ordinary high-grade Japonica rice traded at 20 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen. Overall, prices for mid-grade and lower-grade rice all increased by 1 or 2 jiao. According to these prices, it is the first time ever in Shanghai. Bo Dao also turned upward, and Hakka groups had some transactions, which enlivened the market. Yang Xian still had sources, but the quantity was extremely small, so it was sold out immediately upon arrival. Sales increased by 1 jiao and 5 fen. Du Zi, Ke Bu, and other Xian rice were scarce on the market and also lacked arrivals. Therefore, although they appeared to follow the tightness, there were not many transactions. Bian Yin Yuan rice was consistently firm, with strong buying interest and an excellent situation.

Hu Nan: Goods coming down the river were still scarce, and sales were very brisk. Chang Bang Japonica and Su Tong Japonica rice were frequently raised in price due to rising production prices and special Hakka groups actively purchasing in the producing areas, which caused Lian merchants to wait and see. This affected the source of arrivals in the port. Recently, due to the unrest in the current situation, unscrupulous merchants took the opportunity to profit, causing rice prices to rise repeatedly in both producing and selling areas, endangering the people's food supply. If the authorities in the local and foreign ports do not take measures to provide relief, Shanghai will soon be cut off from supply, and strange market conditions will inevitably appear immediately, and the hidden dangers are worthy of attention. Nan Bang Bo Dao rice saw only a slight firming in prices because store sales and restaurant demand were both average. Yang Du Jian saw the best market conditions because goods were scarce and sales were brisk, raising prices by 2 jiao. Bai Yuan rice saw varying degrees of brisk and slow sales on this street. Sales depended on picking out the higher quality rice. Large quantities followed the general trend and rose by more than 1 jiao. The number of dan traded throughout the day was quite strong, more than the previous day.

Standard Flour Makes More, Soars Again

On the day of the merchant, the various months of the morning, because of foreign grain prices, did a good job of one or two corners, and the people's minds were generally stable, mostly, and still saw the pace of closing in April and May, so that the people inside and outside the industry, no matter what, all had the ears of the rise, until the afternoon, the opening of the market, because of the large number of bulls, the prices were still raised for April, May and June, so all the months were soaring step by step. Most of the big and small factories took this opportunity to sell quite smoothly, and the Tianjin gang also had no gaps. The only goal of the big players is to take advantage of the fact that wheat stocks are running low, and the prices of rice, the main food, are soaring everywhere, so speculators are buying up a lot of wheat, so this kind of price increase seems to be purely man-made, and not due to the mismatch between supply and demand. As a result, this month rose by 1 fen and 7 li half compared with the previous day, April and May rose by 1 fen and 2 li half each, June rose by 1 fen half, July rose by 1 fen, and August rose by 1 fen and 2 li half.

Automotive News Special Article

Pinghan Railway: Introduction to Shunting Design - Zheng Baozhao

In the future, the improvement and development of all new undertakings in our country depend on making full use of the effects of modern scientific inventions. Therefore, the adoption of European and American technologies and systems for railways is indeed a major issue today. However, the key lies in having a long-term vision and meticulous consideration, understanding the current situation and future needs, and then making wise decisions to determine the appropriate policies. Furthermore, a detailed plan should be the standard for implementation, ensuring that facts and theory are perfectly aligned, so that the desired results can be fully achieved.

The train dispatching system is currently the most innovative and perfect system for railway traffic in the world. The remarkable achievements in enhancing transportation capabilities and economic benefits are undeniable. We will leave aside abstract theories and prove it with substantial figures. The London Midland Railway in England adopted the train dispatching system in 1908. According to the railway's statistics, the average weekly train delay time in 1907 was 21,869 hours. After adopting the train dispatching system, it decreased year by year, reaching only 7,749 hours in 1913, a reduction of 64% compared to 1907. The following lists the train delay hours for each year on that railway to demonstrate the improvement of traffic operations:

Average Weekly Delay Hours

1907 21,869

1908 14,501

1909 11,680

1910 9,546

1911 8,959

1912 7,878

1913 7,749

If we further compare the delay time of freight trains during the same period with their revenue, it becomes even more meaningful. In 1907, one hour of freight train delay occurred for every 7 pounds and 8 shillings of revenue. In 1913, one hour of delay occurred for every 22 pounds and 4 shillings. Furthermore, from the perspective of transportation economics, the railway's total freight tonnage in 1913 was 50,500,300 tons, an increase of 3,237,000 tons compared to 1907. The freight revenue in 1913 was 13,297,000 pounds, an increase of 830,750 pounds compared to 1907. However, while tonnage and revenue increased, the train mileage actually decreased by 1,650,000 miles compared to 1907, and coal consumption was reduced by 93,160 tons. Passenger transport also achieved similar results. Due to space limitations, details cannot be listed here. However, even from the comparison of the numbers mentioned above, the improvement in transportation economy and efficiency brought about by the train dispatching system is already astonishing.

This is not unique to the Midland Railway alone. All railways in the British Isles, its territories, and both the European and American continents that have adopted this system have achieved considerable results. If the internal turmoil in our country subsides soon, social order is restored, and various construction projects are implemented in turn, then as a result of the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce, the railway transportation capacity and economy urgently need to be substantially improved. Given the backward state of the existing railways, all locomotives, vehicles, and other equipment must be greatly expanded. The number of trains will become increasingly frequent with the surge in transportation demand. Therefore, the urgent need to adopt the train dispatching system is beyond doubt. However, since the railways in the world that have adopted this system vary greatly in terms of route length, equipment completeness, and the nature and volume of transportation, there are bound to be differences in the extent of their organization, operation, and scope of authority. Before planning to adopt this system for our country's railways, we must conduct a thorough study of the established rules of advanced railways in the world, selecting the most important ones.

Now, let us first discuss the railways in England and its territories.

The railways in the British Isles that have adopted train dispatching include the London Midland and Scottish Railway, the London and North Eastern Railway, and the Great Western Railway.

In other parts of the British Empire, there are some railways in India, the South African Railways, the Federal National Railways of Canada, and the Federal Railway of Malaysia. Although the systems they adopt vary, the scope of duties managed by the dispatching system is generally limited to the following: (1) Ensuring the punctuality of trains. (2) When regular trains are insufficient to meet transportation needs, operating supplementary trains for livestock, perishable goods, and other freight. (3) Utilizing locomotive traction power to achieve complete results, and handling transportation in the most economical way possible within the possible range. (4) Loading trains to the maximum limit. (5) In the event of an accident or track obstruction, changing train routes or canceling trains. (6) Closely considering the volume of transportation, expecting to operate entire trains of freight cars, transporting them over the greatest distance, and reducing stopping points to the minimum. (7) Adjusting the transportation of neighboring large stations. (8) Finding ways to transport goods that cannot be transported by ordinary methods. In addition, there is the expansion of the scope of train dispatching, including the allocation of vehicles, the regulation of loading and unloading matters, the management of the rotation of drivers, firemen, and other train personnel, and the assessment of their work to avoid exceeding hours, as well as the compilation of timetables and traffic diagrams. As for its overall organization, it can be divided into the following four categories: (A) Establishing a central dispatching office to manage the operation of the entire line. (B) Dividing the route into several sections, with a dispatching office established in each section subordinate to the central dispatching office, and the central dispatching office auditing the dispatching matters of each section. (C) Dividing the route into several sub-sections, each with a sub-section dispatching office directly under the jurisdiction of the relevant main section dispatching office. Each main section dispatching office is in turn subordinate to the central dispatching office, as is the case with the Midland and Scottish Railway. (D) Dividing the route into several sections, with a dispatching office established in each section subordinate to the section chief of that section. Some have established a central dispatching office, such as the Great Western Railway, while others have not established a central dispatching office, such as the London and North Western Railway.

Next, let's talk about the railways in the United States.

Most single-track and double-track railways in the United States use the Dispatching System, which directs the transportation affairs of a railway section from a central location. Its main purpose is to operate a large number of trains in the shortest possible time to achieve economic efficiency in operating costs. The Standard Code promulgated by the American Railway Association is a common rule followed by American railways. According to the provisions contained therein, all train dispatching matters are placed under the control of the dispatcher. The dispatcher is subordinate to the chief dispatcher. His ordinary powers are as follows: (A) Ordering the departure of trains. (On single-track lines, he can change the meeting and overtaking locations. On double-track lines, he directs trains to enter sidings or double-track lines, and determines the meeting locations of trains whose schedules have not been determined. Also, to avoid congestion on the lines, he may advance the departure of freight trains when necessary.) (B) Canceling regular trains or special trains. (C) Managing the operation of shunting locomotives, material trains, or worker trains on main lines. (D) Adjusting or supervising train loading according to transportation conditions. (E) Dispatching special trains, shunting locomotives, or rescue trains. In addition, there are dispatchers on some railways who must adjust the transportation of docks and terminal stations. On other railways, the chief dispatcher is responsible for handling this function. There are also dispatchers on some railways who are responsible for handling the shift changes of train personnel. Furthermore, there are dispatchers on some railways who are only responsible for preventing drivers, firemen, and train personnel from violating federal laws. Dispatchers on other railways have no right to interfere in this matter. (To be continued)

News

Hebei's Measures for Collecting Road Maintenance Fees - Wu Fei

After a road is built, in order to benefit from it permanently, maintenance is essential. However, road maintenance relies on funding, so the source of funding is naturally an important issue. Recently, Hebei Province has formulated twelve articles of regulations for collecting road maintenance fees, which have been approved by the provincial government and implemented. After examining the measures, they are worthy of emulation. I have recorded the main points here for guidance. According to Article 7 of the organizational outline, the Hebei Provincial Road Bureau collects road maintenance fees. Therefore, the provincial roads are divided into three grades: first-grade roads are those with high traffic volume and difficult maintenance, second-grade roads are those with low traffic volume and easier maintenance, and third-grade roads are those that have been leveled and padded from existing official roads and can be used by cars. The vehicles allowed to travel on provincial roads are limited to seven types: cars, four-wheeled carriages, flat-wheeled carts, flat-wheeled sedan chairs, electric bicycles, bicycles, and rickshaws. All other vehicles and livestock are not allowed to pass. Therefore, according to the grade of the road and the type of vehicle, all vehicles traveling on provincial roads shall pay road maintenance fees according to the prescribed rates: (A) Cars: For first-grade passenger cars with 20 to 30 seats, the road maintenance fee is $1.10 per Chinese mile per month; for second-grade passenger cars with 10 to 20 seats, the road maintenance fee is $0.80 per Chinese mile per month; for third-grade passenger cars with less than 10 seats, the road maintenance fee is $0.50 per

Page 30

Chinese mile per month. The road maintenance fees for first-grade freight cars with 2 to 3 tons, second-grade freight cars with 1 to 2 tons, and third-grade freight cars with less than 1 ton shall be the same as those for the above three types of passenger cars of the same grade. In addition, for cars traveling on first-grade provincial roads within 100 Chinese miles, the road maintenance fee shall be charged according to the above-mentioned rates; from 101 to 200 Chinese miles, the monthly road maintenance fee shall be reduced by 5%; from 201 to 300 Chinese miles, the monthly road maintenance fee shall be reduced by 10%; and from 301 to 400 Chinese miles, the monthly road maintenance fee shall be reduced by 15%. Those traveling on second-grade roads shall be charged 70% of the fee, and those traveling on third-grade roads shall be charged 50% of the fee. (B) Four-wheeled carriages shall be charged $13 per month. (C) Flat-wheeled carts with a double team shall be charged $6 per month, and those with a single team shall be charged $3 per month. (D) Flat-wheeled sedan chairs shall be charged $3 per month. (E) Electric bicycles shall be charged $12 per month. (F) Rickshaws shall be charged $0.50 per month. From this, we can see that the amount of the fee is determined by the distance traveled, and the standard for collection is determined by the type of vehicle. Moreover, all these vehicles, regardless of which grade of provincial road they travel on, shall be charged separately according to this example, which can be said to be in accordance with legal principles and appropriate. However, there is no supervision of the vehicles traveling, so it is stipulated that vehicles traveling on provincial roads must apply to the responsible provincial road bureau for a license plate on a monthly basis, indicating it on the vehicle for inspection. Those without a license plate are not allowed to pass. If business cars must first apply to the relevant provincial road bureau for registration and obtain a license before applying for a license plate. The registration rules for long-distance business cars will be separately stipulated. After various vehicles have been registered and approved and issued a license, they shall exchange their license plates monthly and pay the full monthly road maintenance fee at once. If anyone does not obtain a license plate or fails to exchange it after it has expired, and travels privately, once discovered, in addition to obtaining a license plate and paying the normal fee, they shall also be fined one to three times the amount of the fee. For various private cars that pass temporarily, the road maintenance fee shall be charged at three-quarters of the above-mentioned rates calculated daily. If charitable organizations and government agencies use vehicles for relief or to facilitate paperwork, and they must pass through provincial roads, they may be exempted from road maintenance fees if they notify the relevant provincial road bureau in advance and obtain a license. In addition, if county road bureaus build roads and the construction costs are high, and road maintenance also requires collection, the county governments may stipulate and submit it to the provincial construction department for approval and record. All of the above are Hebei Province's measures for collecting road maintenance fees. Various places can extract the strengths of the regulations and stipulate the collection of road maintenance fees according to local conditions so that the construction of roads always has funding and is free from the danger of road surface collapse and increased danger.

Shandong Purchases Long-Distance Buses - Ji Ren

Shandong Chairman Chen Tiaoyuan, in view of the importance of road administration and the convenience of automobile transportation, specially sent representative Mr. Chen to Shanghai to purchase 150 General Motors long-distance buses from the American General Motors Company at a value of more than 300,000 yuan to expand roads and promote automobile traffic. The plan should be welcomed by all sectors.

The American General Motors Company has always had the goal of promoting transportation and road administration in various countries, so it has established branches around the world. There are also two branches in China, one in Shanghai and one in Shenyang. ‧It is responsible for designing automobile roads in China and has already made great efforts‧. Now it is working harder and serving conscientiously. It has also appointed managers in various places to specialize in selling various General Motors cars. It has established parts and service stations in Shanghai to specialize in vehicle repair‧. Whether it is public or private, General Motors is thinking of the convenience of its customers. This is why General Motors Company has gained the trust of society and the support of all sectors. The world's largest capital and best service automobile manufacturer is none other than General Motors.

The above picture shows Representative Chen and the manager of the Shanghai branch of the American General Motors Company taking a group photo at the branch when discussing prices and placing orders to commemorate the occasion.
